=== Example 78 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
FOL: all x. (Taxpayer(x) -> ContributeTo(x, Country))
TEXT: Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
FOL: all x. (WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency) -> Taxpayer(x))
TEXT: Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
FOL: all x. (ServesIn(x, TheArmy) -> WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency))
TEXT: Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
FOL: all x. (SentencedForMurder(x) -> Imprisoned(x))
TEXT: Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
FOL: all x. (Imprisoned((x) -> Has(x, CriminalRecord))
TEXT: James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
FOL: ((SentencedForMurder(James) & -Imprisoned(James)) | (-SentencedForMurder(James) & Imprisoned(James)))
TEXT: James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
FOL: ((Has(James, CriminalRecord) & -Taxpayer(James)) | (-Has(James, CriminalRecord) & Taxpayer(James)))
TEXT: James does not contribute to the country.
FOL: ContributeToCountry(James)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: No songs are visuals.
FOL: all x. (Song(x) -> -Visual(x))
TEXT: All folk songs are songs.
FOL: all x. (FolkSong(x) -> Song(x))
TEXT: All videos are visuals.
FOL: all x. (Video(x) -> Visual(x))
TEXT: All movies are videos.
FOL: all x. (Movie(x) -> Video(x))
TEXT: All sci-fi movies are movies.
FOL: all x. (ScifiMovie(x) -> Movie(x))
TEXT: Inception is a sci-fi movie.
FOL: ScifiMovie(Inception)
TEXT: Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
FOL: -FolkSong(Mac) & -ScifiMovie(Mac)
TEXT: Inception is a folk song.
FOL: FolkSong(Inception)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: Every chef can cook.
FOL: all x. (Chef(x) -> Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
FOL: exists x. (-Chef(x) & Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
FOL: all x. (Can(x, Cook) -> (CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(x, Pasta)))
TEXT: If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
FOL: all x. (CanMake(x, Cookies) & CanMake(x, Muffins) -> Baker(x))
TEXT: Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
FOL: all x. ((Baker(x) & CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs)) -> CanMake(x, GoodBreakfast))
TEXT: Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
FOL: CanMake(Luke, Cookies) & (CanMake(Luke, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(Luke, Muffins) & -CanMake(Luke, Pasta)
TEXT: Luke is a chef.
FOL: MakeGoodBreakfast(Luke)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
FOL: exists x. exists y. (Develop(eTS, x) & Develop(eTS, y) & StandardizedTest(x) & StandardizedTest(y) & In(x, UnitedState) & In(y, UnitedState) & For(x, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation) & For(y, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation))
TEXT: ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
FOL: exists x. (Administer(eTS, x) & InternationalTest(x) & (TOEFL(x) | TOEIC(x) | GRE(x) | SubjectTest(x)))
TEXT: Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
FOL: exists x. (Develop(eTS, x) & AssociatedWith(x, EntryToUSEducationInstitution))
TEXT: ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
FOL: exists x. (Develop(eTS, x) & StateWideAssesment(x) & UsedFor(x, AccountabilityTesting))
TEXT: ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
FOL: exists x. (Develops(Ets, x) & For(x, k-OneTwoandhighereducation)) & exists x. (Develops(Ets, x) & AssociatedWith(x, Entrytouseducationinstitutions))

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.
Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.
FOL: Actor(DaveedDiggs) & FilmProducer(DaveedDiggs)
TEXT: Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
FOL: exists x. exists y.(PlaysIn(DaveedDiggs, x, Hamilton) & (-(x=y)) & PlaysIn(DaveedDiggs, y, Hamilton)) & OnBroadway(Hamilton) & Musical(Hamilton)
TEXT: One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. exists y.(Actor(x) & PlaysIn(x, y, Hamilton) & Wins(x, BestActorAward))
TEXT: The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. (Actor(x) & PlaysIn(x, ThomasJefferson, Hamilton) & Wins(x, BestActorAward))
TEXT: Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
FOL: Plays(DaveedDiggs, ThomasJefferson)
TEXT: Musicals on Broadway are not films.
FOL: all x. ((Musical(x) & OnBroadway(x)) -> -Film(x))
TEXT: Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. (BRICS(x) & Speaks(x, Hindi))

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
The dog does not eat the mouse.
The dog does not eat the tiger.
The dog is round.
The dog likes the lion.
The dog likes the mouse.
The lion eats the tiger.
The mouse is not cold.
The mouse is round.
The mouse needs the dog.
The tiger is blue.
The tiger is rough.
The tiger does not need the lion.
If someone likes the mouse and they are blue then the mouse eats the dog.
If someone likes the mouse and the mouse is blue then the mouse is rough.
If someone is cold then they need the tiger.
If someone eats the lion then they need the tiger.
If someone likes the dog then they are rough.
If someone is blue and they eat the lion then the lion is rough.
If someone is rough then they eat the lion.
If someone needs the tiger then they do not like the lion.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The mouse eats the lion.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the given premises and the conclusion into first-order logic (FOL) expressions and then evaluate the conclusion based on the premises.

### Translation of Premises:
1. **The dog does not eat the mouse.**
   - FOL: ¬Eats(Dog, Mouse)
   
2. **The dog does not eat the tiger.**
   - FOL: ¬Eats(Dog, Tiger)
   
3. **The dog is round.**
   - FOL: Round(Dog)
   
4. **The dog likes the lion.**
   - FOL: Likes(Dog, Lion)
   
5. **The dog likes the mouse.**
   - FOL: Likes(Dog, Mouse)
   
6. **The lion eats the tiger.**
   - FOL: Eats(Lion, Tiger)
   
7. **The mouse is not cold.**
   - FOL: ¬Cold(Mouse)
   
8. **The mouse is round.**
   - FOL: Round(Mouse)
   
9. **The mouse needs the dog.**
   - FOL: Needs(Mouse, Dog)
   
10. **The tiger is blue.**
    - FOL: Blue(Tiger)
    
11. **The tiger is rough.**
    - FOL: Rough(Tiger)
    
12. **The tiger does not need the lion.**
    - FOL: ¬Needs(Tiger, Lion)
    
13. **If someone likes the mouse and they are blue then the mouse eats the dog.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Likes(x, Mouse) ∧ Blue(x) → Eats(Mouse, Dog))
    
14. **If someone likes the mouse and the mouse is blue then the mouse is rough.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Likes(x, Mouse) ∧ Blue(Mouse) → Rough(Mouse))
    
15. **If someone is cold then they need the tiger.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Cold(x) → Needs(x, Tiger))
    
16. **If someone eats the lion then they need the tiger.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Eats(x, Lion) → Needs(x, Tiger))
    
17. **If someone likes the dog then they are rough.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Likes(x, Dog) → Rough(x))
    
18. **If someone is blue and they eat the lion then the lion is rough.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Blue(x) ∧ Eats(x, Lion) → Rough(Lion))
    
19. **If someone is rough then they eat the lion.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Rough(x) → Eats(x, Lion))
    
20. **If someone needs the tiger then they do not like the lion.**
    - FOL: ∀x (Needs(x, Tiger) → ¬Likes(x, Lion))

### Conclusion:
**The mouse eats the lion.**
- FOL: Eats(Mouse, Lion)

### Evaluation:
We need to determine if the conclusion logically follows from the premises.

From premise 7, we know that the mouse is not cold (¬Cold(Mouse)). Therefore, premise 15 (If someone is cold then they need the tiger) does not apply directly to the mouse.

Premise 17 states that if someone likes the dog, then they are rough. From premise 5, we know that the dog likes the mouse (Likes(Dog, Mouse)). However, this does not imply that the mouse likes the dog. Hence, we cannot directly use premise 17 to infer anything about the roughness of the mouse.

Premise 14 states that if someone likes the mouse and the mouse is blue, then the mouse is rough. We know the mouse is round (premise 8), but we don't have information about the mouse being blue. Hence, we cannot use this premise to infer that the mouse is rough.

Premise 18 states that if someone is blue and they eat the lion, then the lion is rough. We do not have information that the mouse is blue, so this premise does not help us determine the roughness of the lion.

Premise 19 states that if someone is rough, then they eat the lion. Since we cannot establish that the mouse is rough, we cannot conclude that the mouse eats the lion from this premise.

Given the premises, there is no direct logical path to conclude that "the mouse eats the lion." None of the premises provide a sufficient condition to establish this conclusion.

### Final Answer:
ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: Uncertain

=== Example 79 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.

TEXT: If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
FOL: all x. (CanMake(x, Cookies) & CanMake(x, Muffins) -> Baker(x))
TEXT: Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
FOL: all x. ((Baker(x) & CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs)) -> CanMake(x, GoodBreakfast))
TEXT: Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
FOL: CanMake(Luke, Cookies) & (CanMake(Luke, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(Luke, Muffins) & -CanMake(Luke, Pasta)
TEXT: Luke is a chef.
FOL: MakeGoodBreakfast(Luke)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))

TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
The bald eagle eats the squirrel.
The bald eagle is kind.
The bald eagle is round.
The bald eagle does not visit the squirrel.
The cat is rough.
The cat likes the squirrel.
The cow is big.
The cow likes the squirrel.
The cow visits the squirrel.
The squirrel eats the cow.
The squirrel likes the bald eagle.
If someone likes the cow and they do not eat the cat then they do not eat the bald eagle.
If someone eats the cat then they are blue.
If someone is big then they do not like the cat.
If the cow eats the cat and the cat is big then the cow visits the bald eagle.
If someone visits the cat then the cat is round.
If someone visits the cow then they are round.
If someone is kind then they like the squirrel.
If someone visits the cat and the cat is round then they are big.
If someone eats the squirrel and they like the squirrel then the squirrel visits the cat.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The squirrel does not like the cat.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate each premise and the conclusion into FOL expressions, and then evaluate whether the conclusion logically follows from the premises.

### Translation

**Premises:**
1. The bald eagle eats the squirrel.
   - FOL: `Eats(BaldEagle, Squirrel)`
2. The bald eagle is kind.
   - FOL: `Kind(BaldEagle)`
3. The bald eagle is round.
   - FOL: `Round(BaldEagle)`
4. The bald eagle does not visit the squirrel.
   - FOL: `-Visits(BaldEagle, Squirrel)`
5. The cat is rough.
   - FOL: `Rough(Cat)`
6. The cat likes the squirrel.
   - FOL: `Likes(Cat, Squirrel)`
7. The cow is big.
   - FOL: `Big(Cow)`
8. The cow likes the squirrel.
   - FOL: `Likes(Cow, Squirrel)`
9. The cow visits the squirrel.
   - FOL: `Visits(Cow, Squirrel)`
10. The squirrel eats the cow.
    - FOL: `Eats(Squirrel, Cow)`
11. The squirrel likes the bald eagle.
    - FOL: `Likes(Squirrel, BaldEagle)`
12. If someone likes the cow and they do not eat the cat then they do not eat the bald eagle.
    - FOL: `all x. (Likes(x, Cow) & -Eats(x, Cat) -> -Eats(x, BaldEagle))`
13. If someone eats the cat then they are blue.
    - FOL: `all x. (Eats(x, Cat) -> Blue(x))`
14. If someone is big then they do not like the cat.
    - FOL: `all x. (Big(x) -> -Likes(x, Cat))`
15. If the cow eats the cat and the cat is big then the cow visits the bald eagle.
    - FOL: `(Eats(Cow, Cat) & Big(Cat) -> Visits(Cow, BaldEagle))`
16. If someone visits the cat then the cat is round.
    - FOL: `all x. (Visits(x, Cat) -> Round(Cat))`
17. If someone visits the cow then they are round.
    - FOL: `all x. (Visits(x, Cow) -> Round(x))`
18. If someone is kind then they like the squirrel.
    - FOL: `all x. (Kind(x) -> Likes(x, Squirrel))`
19. If someone visits the cat and the cat is round then they are big.
    - FOL: `all x. (Visits(x, Cat) & Round(Cat) -> Big(x))`
20. If someone eats the squirrel and they like the squirrel then the squirrel visits the cat.
    - FOL: `all x. (Eats(x, Squirrel) & Likes(x, Squirrel) -> Visits(Squirrel, Cat))`

**Conclusion:**
- The squirrel does not like the cat.
  - FOL: `-Likes(Squirrel, Cat)`

### Evaluation

From the premises:
- We know that the squirrel likes the bald eagle (`Likes(Squirrel, BaldEagle)`).
- The cat likes the squirrel (`Likes(Cat, Squirrel)`).

However, there is no direct information provided about the squirrel liking the cat. To determine whether the squirrel likes the cat or not, we would need additional information or a rule that directly links the squirrel's feelings towards the cat.

Given the premises, none of the rules or statements directly imply or contradict the conclusion `-Likes(Squirrel, Cat)`.

Thus, based on the provided premises:

**ANSWER: Uncertain**
Processed: Uncertain

Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
FOL: all x. (Taxpayer(x) -> ContributeTo(x, Country))
TEXT: Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
FOL: all x. (WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency) -> Taxpayer(x))
TEXT: Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
FOL: all x. (ServesIn(x, TheArmy) -> WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency))
TEXT: Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
FOL: all x. (SentencedForMurder(x) -> Imprisoned(x))
TEXT: Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
FOL: all x. (Imprisoned((x) -> Has(x, CriminalRecord))
TEXT: James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
FOL: ((SentencedForMurder(James) & -Imprisoned(James)) | (-SentencedForMurder(James) & Imprisoned(James)))
TEXT: James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
FOL: ((Has(James, CriminalRecord) & -Taxpayer(James)) | (-Has(James, CriminalRecord) & Taxpayer(James)))
TEXT: James does not contribute to the country.
FOL: ContributeToCountry(James)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

All folk songs are songs.

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Chef(x) -> Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
FOL: exists x. (-Chef(x) & Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
FOL: all x. (Can(x, Cook) -> (CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(x, Pasta)))
TEXT: If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.

TEXT: Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
FOL: all x. ((Baker(x) & CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs)) -> CanMake(x, GoodBreakfast))
TEXT: Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.

TEXT: Luke is a chef.

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
FOL: exists x. exists y. (Develop(eTS, x) & Develop(eTS, y) & StandardizedTest(x) & StandardizedTest(y) & In(x, UnitedState) & In(y, UnitedState) & For(x, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation) & For(y, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation))
TEXT: ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
FOL: exists x. (Administer(eTS, x) & InternationalTest(x) & (TOEFL(x) | TOEIC(x) | GRE(x) | SubjectTest(x)))
TEXT: Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.

TEXT: ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.

TEXT: ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.
Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: Actor(DaveedDiggs) & FilmProducer(DaveedDiggs)
TEXT: Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
FOL: exists x. exists y.(PlaysIn(DaveedDiggs, x, Hamilton) & (-(x=y)) & PlaysIn(DaveedDiggs, y, Hamilton)) & OnBroadway(Hamilton) & Musical(Hamilton)
TEXT: One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. exists y.(Actor(x) & PlaysIn(x, y, Hamilton) & Wins(x, BestActorAward))
TEXT: The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. (Actor(x) & PlaysIn(x, ThomasJefferson, Hamilton) & Wins(x, BestActorAward))
TEXT: Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
FOL: Plays(DaveedDiggs, ThomasJefferson)
TEXT: Musicals on Broadway are not films.
FOL: all x. ((Musical(x) & OnBroadway(x)) -> -Film(x))
TEXT: Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. (BRICS(x) & Speaks(x, Hindi))

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Charlie is cold.
Charlie is furry.
Charlie is smart.
Dave is furry.
Dave is young.
Gary is quiet.
Gary is smart.
Harry is furry.
Harry is quiet.
Harry is young.
If someone is cold and quiet then they are white.
If someone is cold and big then they are young.
All furry people are white.
Quiet people are cold.
If someone is furry then they are white.
If someone is smart and white then they are furry.
All furry people are big.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Harry is not cold.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate each premise and the conclusion into first-order logic (FOL) expressions:

**Premises:**
1. Charlie is cold.
   - FOL: Cold(Charlie)
2. Charlie is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Charlie)
3. Charlie is smart.
   - FOL: Smart(Charlie)
4. Dave is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Dave)
5. Dave is young.
   - FOL: Young(Dave)
6. Gary is quiet.
   - FOL: Quiet(Gary)
7. Gary is smart.
   - FOL: Smart(Gary)
8. Harry is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Harry)
9. Harry is quiet.
   - FOL: Quiet(Harry)
10. Harry is young.
    - FOL: Young(Harry)
11. If someone is cold and quiet then they are white.
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) & Quiet(x) -> White(x))
12. If someone is cold and big then they are young.
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) & Big(x) -> Young(x))
13. All furry people are white.
    - FOL: all x. (Furry(x) -> White(x))
14. Quiet people are cold.
    - FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) -> Cold(x))
15. If someone is furry then they are white.
    - FOL: all x. (Furry(x) -> White(x))
16. If someone is smart and white then they are furry.
    - FOL: all x. (Smart(x) & White(x) -> Furry(x))
17. All furry people are big.
    - FOL: all x. (Furry(x) -> Big(x))

**Conclusion:**
- Harry is not cold.
  - FOL: -Cold(Harry)

**Evaluation:**

First, we will derive information about Harry based on the given premises:
- From premise 9: Quiet(Harry)
- From premise 14: Quiet(x) -> Cold(x), thus Quiet(Harry) -> Cold(Harry)
- Hence, we can infer that Harry is cold: Cold(Harry).

Given this derivation, the statement "Harry is not cold" directly contradicts our inference. Therefore, the conclusion does not follow from the premises.

**Answer:**
- ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 82 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Bob is nice.
Charlie is round.
Gary is blue.
Gary is nice.
Gary is rough.
Gary is round.
Harry is blue.
Harry is nice.
Harry is quiet.
Harry is rough.
All quiet, round people are young.
All young, blue people are rough.
All round, big people are young.
Blue people are round.
All rough people are quiet.
If someone is big then they are rough.
If someone is quiet and big then they are round.
If Charlie is nice and Charlie is big then Charlie is blue.
All nice people are big.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Bob is blue.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the provided premises and evaluate the conclusion:

**Premises in FOL:**
1. Bob is nice.
   FOL: Nice(Bob)
2. Charlie is round.
   FOL: Round(Charlie)
3. Gary is blue.
   FOL: Blue(Gary)
4. Gary is nice.
   FOL: Nice(Gary)
5. Gary is rough.
   FOL: Rough(Gary)
6. Gary is round.
   FOL: Round(Gary)
7. Harry is blue.
   FOL: Blue(Harry)
8. Harry is nice.
   FOL: Nice(Harry)
9. Harry is quiet.
   FOL: Quiet(Harry)
10. Harry is rough.
    FOL: Rough(Harry)
11. All quiet, round people are young.
    FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) & Round(x) -> Young(x))
12. All young, blue people are rough.
    FOL: all x. (Young(x) & Blue(x) -> Rough(x))
13. All round, big people are young.
    FOL: all x. (Round(x) & Big(x) -> Young(x))
14. Blue people are round.
    FOL: all x. (Blue(x) -> Round(x))
15. All rough people are quiet.
    FOL: all x. (Rough(x) -> Quiet(x))
16. If someone is big then they are rough.
    FOL: all x. (Big(x) -> Rough(x))
17. If someone is quiet and big then they are round.
    FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) & Big(x) -> Round(x))
18. If Charlie is nice and Charlie is big then Charlie is blue.
    FOL: (Nice(Charlie) & Big(Charlie) -> Blue(Charlie))
19. All nice people are big.
    FOL: all x. (Nice(x) -> Big(x))

**Conclusion in FOL:**
- Bob is blue.
  FOL: Blue(Bob)

**Evaluation:**

From premise 1, we know:
- Nice(Bob)

From premise 19, we infer:
- Nice(Bob) -> Big(Bob), so Big(Bob).

From premise 16, since Bob is big:
- Big(Bob) -> Rough(Bob), so Rough(Bob).

From premise 15, since Bob is rough:
- Rough(Bob) -> Quiet(Bob), so Quiet(Bob).

From premise 11, since Bob is quiet and big:
- Quiet(Bob) & Big(Bob) -> Round(Bob), so Round(Bob).

From premise 14, since Bob is round:
- Round(Bob) does not directly imply Blue(Bob).

There is no direct information linking Bob's roundness to being blue based on the premises given.

Thus, we cannot conclude that Bob is blue based on the premises.

**Final Answer:**
ANSWER: Uncertain
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain
========================================

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.

All woodware is biodegradable.

A worksheet is not biodegradable.

<EVALUATE>

TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))

TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.

<PREMISES>

Every chef can cook.

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
FOL: exists x. exists y. (Develop(eTS, x) & Develop(eTS, y) & StandardizedTest(x) & StandardizedTest(y) & In(x, UnitedState) & In(y, UnitedState) & For(x, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation) & For(y, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation))

TEXT: ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.

TEXT: ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
FOL: exists x. (Develops(Ets, x) & For(x, k-OneTwoandhighereducation)) & exists x. (Develops(Ets, x) & AssociatedWith(x, Entrytouseducationinstitutions))

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.

One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.

Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>

Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.

TEXT: The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.

TEXT: Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. (BRICS(x) & Speaks(x, Hindi))

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Anne is cold.
Charlie is furry.
Charlie is round.
Fiona is quiet.
Gary is nice.
Gary is quiet.
Gary is round.
Nice people are white.
All round, cold people are nice.
If someone is furry and round then they are cold.
All cold, green people are quiet.
If Charlie is cold then Charlie is nice.
If someone is furry and white then they are green.
If Anne is white and Anne is quiet then Anne is green.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Charlie is white.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the given premises into First Order Logic (FOL) expressions and then evaluate the conclusion.

**Premises:**

1. **Anne is cold.**
   FOL: Cold(Anne)

2. **Charlie is furry.**
   FOL: Furry(Charlie)

3. **Charlie is round.**
   FOL: Round(Charlie)

4. **Fiona is quiet.**
   FOL: Quiet(Fiona)

5. **Gary is nice.**
   FOL: Nice(Gary)

6. **Gary is quiet.**
   FOL: Quiet(Gary)

7. **Gary is round.**
   FOL: Round(Gary)

8. **Nice people are white.**
   FOL: all x. (Nice(x) -> White(x))

9. **All round, cold people are nice.**
   FOL: all x. (Round(x) & Cold(x) -> Nice(x))

10. **If someone is furry and round then they are cold.**
    FOL: all x. (Furry(x) & Round(x) -> Cold(x))

11. **All cold, green people are quiet.**
    FOL: all x. (Cold(x) & Green(x) -> Quiet(x))

12. **If Charlie is cold then Charlie is nice.**
    FOL: Cold(Charlie) -> Nice(Charlie)

13. **If someone is furry and white then they are green.**
    FOL: all x. (Furry(x) & White(x) -> Green(x))

14. **If Anne is white and Anne is quiet then Anne is green.**
    FOL: (White(Anne) & Quiet(Anne)) -> Green(Anne)

**Conclusion:**

15. **Charlie is white.**
    FOL: White(Charlie)

**Evaluation:**

First, let's analyze the premises step-by-step:

- From premise 2 and 3, we know Charlie is furry and round.
- From premise 10, since Charlie is furry and round, we can infer that Charlie is cold.
  - Furry(Charlie) & Round(Charlie) -> Cold(Charlie)

- Now, from premise 9, since Charlie is round and cold, Charlie must be nice.
  - Round(Charlie) & Cold(Charlie) -> Nice(Charlie)

- From premise 8, since Charlie is nice, Charlie must be white.
  - Nice(Charlie) -> White(Charlie)

Thus, based on the logical deductions from the premises, Charlie is indeed white.

**Answer: True**

Charlie being white follows directly from the given premises.
Processed: True

Reference: True

=== Example 84 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

If something needs the dog and the dog needs the cat then the cat sees the tiger.
If something sees the dog then it visits the cat.
If something sees the tiger and the tiger is red then it needs the cat.
If something sees the tiger and the tiger sees the dog then the tiger visits the dog.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The tiger needs the cat.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the premises and evaluate the conclusion step-by-step.

### Premises:
1. **The cat is red.**
   - FOL: Red(Cat)
2. **The cat needs the cow.**
   - FOL: Needs(Cat, Cow)
3. **The cow is red.**
   - FOL: Red(Cow)
4. **The cow needs the cat.**
   - FOL: Needs(Cow, Cat)
5. **The cow sees the cat.**
   - FOL: Sees(Cow, Cat)
6. **The cow does not see the dog.**
   - FOL: -Sees(Cow, Dog)
7. **The cow sees the tiger.**
   - FOL: Sees(Cow, Tiger)
8. **The dog is blue.**
   - FOL: Blue(Dog)
9. **The dog needs the cow.**
   - FOL: Needs(Dog, Cow)
10. **The dog does not need the tiger.**
    - FOL: -Needs(Dog, Tiger)
11. **The dog sees the tiger.**
    - FOL: Sees(Dog, Tiger)
12. **The dog visits the cat.**
    - FOL: Visits(Dog, Cat)
13. **The dog visits the cow.**
    - FOL: Visits(Dog, Cow)
14. **The tiger is cold.**
    - FOL: Cold(Tiger)
15. **The tiger sees the cat.**
    - FOL: Sees(Tiger, Cat)
16. **The tiger sees the cow.**
    - FOL: Sees(Tiger, Cow)
17. **If something is cold and blue then it sees the dog.**
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) & Blue(x) -> Sees(x, Dog))
18. **If something visits the dog then the dog visits the tiger.**
    - FOL: all x. (Visits(x, Dog) -> Visits(Dog, Tiger))
19. **If something needs the cat then the cat visits the dog.**
    - FOL: all x. (Needs(x, Cat) -> Visits(Cat, Dog))
20. **If something visits the tiger then the tiger is blue.**
    - FOL: all x. (Visits(x, Tiger) -> Blue(Tiger))
21. **If something needs the dog and the dog needs the cat then the cat sees the tiger.**
    - FOL: all x. (Needs(x, Dog) & Needs(Dog, Cat) -> Sees(Cat, Tiger))
22. **If something sees the dog then it visits the cat.**
    - FOL: all x. (Sees(x, Dog) -> Visits(x, Cat))
23. **If something sees the tiger and the tiger is red then it needs the cat.**
    - FOL: all x. (Sees(x, Tiger) & Red(Tiger) -> Needs(x, Cat))
24. **If something sees the tiger and the tiger sees the dog then the tiger visits the dog.**
    - FOL: all x. (Sees(x, Tiger) & Sees(Tiger, Dog) -> Visits(Tiger, Dog))

### Conclusion:
**The tiger needs the cat.**
- FOL: Needs(Tiger, Cat)

### Evaluation:
From the premises, we have:
- **Red(Cat)** (Premise 1)
- **Sees(Tiger, Cat)** (Premise 15)
- **Sees(Tiger, Cow)** (Premise 16)
- **Cold(Tiger)** (Premise 14)

We need to check if the tiger needs the cat based on these premises.

From premise 23:
- **If something sees the tiger and the tiger is red then it needs the cat.**
  - FOL: all x. (Sees(x, Tiger) & Red(Tiger) -> Needs(x, Cat))

However, we do not have information about the color of the tiger:
- **Red(Tiger)** is not given.

Since the tiger is not necessarily red, we cannot conclude that the tiger needs the cat based on this rule.

Thus, the conclusion **"The tiger needs the cat"** does not follow from the given premises.

**ANSWER: False**
Processed: False

Reference: Uncertain

=== Example 85 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))

FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
The cow likes the lion.
The cow likes the mouse.
The cow likes the squirrel.
The lion eats the mouse.
The lion is green.
The lion likes the squirrel.
The mouse is blue.
The mouse likes the cow.
The mouse visits the lion.
The squirrel visits the cow.
If someone visits the cow then they eat the mouse.
If someone likes the mouse then they visit the lion.
If someone visits the cow then they eat the cow.
If someone visits the squirrel and the squirrel is blue then the squirrel likes the cow.
If someone is cold then they eat the cow.
If someone is green then they are big.
If someone is big and green then they like the lion.
If someone likes the lion then they are cold.
If someone eats the cow then they visit the cow.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The mouse is cold.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the premises and evaluate the conclusion.

### Premises:
1. **The cow likes the lion.**
   - `Likes(Cow, Lion)`
2. **The cow likes the mouse.**
   - `Likes(Cow, Mouse)`
3. **The cow likes the squirrel.**
   - `Likes(Cow, Squirrel)`
4. **The lion eats the mouse.**
   - `Eats(Lion, Mouse)`
5. **The lion is green.**
   - `Green(Lion)`
6. **The lion likes the squirrel.**
   - `Likes(Lion, Squirrel)`
7. **The mouse is blue.**
   - `Blue(Mouse)`
8. **The mouse likes the cow.**
   - `Likes(Mouse, Cow)`
9. **The mouse visits the lion.**
   - `Visits(Mouse, Lion)`
10. **The squirrel visits the cow.**
    - `Visits(Squirrel, Cow)`
11. **If someone visits the cow then they eat the mouse.**
    - `all x. (Visits(x, Cow) -> Eats(x, Mouse))`
12. **If someone likes the mouse then they visit the lion.**
    - `all x. (Likes(x, Mouse) -> Visits(x, Lion))`
13. **If someone visits the cow then they eat the cow.**
    - `all x. (Visits(x, Cow) -> Eats(x, Cow))`
14. **If someone visits the squirrel and the squirrel is blue then the squirrel likes the cow.**
    - `all x. (Visits(x, Squirrel) & Blue(Squirrel) -> Likes(Squirrel, Cow))`
15. **If someone is cold then they eat the cow.**
    - `all x. (Cold(x) -> Eats(x, Cow))`
16. **If someone is green then they are big.**
    - `all x. (Green(x) -> Big(x))`
17. **If someone is big and green then they like the lion.**
    - `all x. (Big(x) & Green(x) -> Likes(x, Lion))`
18. **If someone likes the lion then they are cold.**
    - `all x. (Likes(x, Lion) -> Cold(x))`
19. **If someone eats the cow then they visit the cow.**
    - `all x. (Eats(x, Cow) -> Visits(x, Cow))`

### Conclusion:
**The mouse is cold.**
- `Cold(Mouse)`

### Analysis:
1. From premise 9, we know `Visits(Mouse, Lion)` is true.
2. According to premise 11, since `Visits(Mouse, Cow)` would imply `Eats(Mouse, Mouse)`, which is not stated or implied by any other premise, we need to check other implications.
3. Premise 12 states that if `Likes(x, Mouse)`, then `Visits(x, Lion)`. Since `Likes(Mouse, Cow)` is given, this implies `Visits(Mouse, Lion)`, which is already true.
4. We need to determine if `Mouse` being cold (`Cold(Mouse)`) can be derived from the premises.
5. To determine if `Mouse` is cold, we need to find a chain that links `Mouse` to the conditions leading to being cold.
6. Since no direct link to `Mouse` being cold is provided, and the premises do not establish any connection between `Mouse` and `Cold`, we cannot conclude that `Mouse` is cold based on the given information.

### Conclusion:
Since there is no direct or indirect implication in the premises that leads us to conclude `Cold(Mouse)`, the answer is:

**ANSWER: Uncertain**

This is because the premises do not provide enough information to definitively state that the mouse is cold.

All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: No songs are visuals.
FOL: all x. (Song(x) -> -Visual(x))
TEXT: All folk songs are songs.
FOL: all x. (FolkSong(x) -> Song(x))
TEXT: All videos are visuals.
FOL: all x. (Video(x) -> Visual(x))
TEXT: All movies are videos.
FOL: all x. (Movie(x) -> Video(x))
TEXT: All sci-fi movies are movies.
FOL: all x. (ScifiMovie(x) -> Movie(x))
TEXT: Inception is a sci-fi movie.
FOL: ScifiMovie(Inception)
TEXT: Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
FOL: -FolkSong(Mac) & -ScifiMovie(Mac)
TEXT: Inception is a folk song.
FOL: FolkSong(Inception)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: Every chef can cook.
FOL: all x. (Chef(x) -> Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
FOL: exists x. (-Chef(x) & Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
FOL: all x. (Can(x, Cook) -> (CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(x, Pasta)))
TEXT: If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
FOL: all x. (CanMake(x, Cookies) & CanMake(x, Muffins) -> Baker(x))
TEXT: Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
FOL: all x. ((Baker(x) & CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs)) -> CanMake(x, GoodBreakfast))
TEXT: Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
FOL: CanMake(Luke, Cookies) & (CanMake(Luke, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(Luke, Muffins) & -CanMake(Luke, Pasta)
TEXT: Luke is a chef.
FOL: MakeGoodBreakfast(Luke)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.

ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.

Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.

TEXT: Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
The bald eagle chases the dog.
The bald eagle is green.
The bald eagle visits the squirrel.
The dog chases the rabbit.
The dog likes the squirrel.
The rabbit chases the bald eagle.
The rabbit is rough.
The rabbit likes the squirrel.
The rabbit visits the squirrel.
The squirrel likes the bald eagle.
If someone likes the dog then the dog is round.
If someone chases the rabbit then the rabbit does not visit the dog.
If someone likes the dog then they are rough.
If someone likes the dog then they are green.
If someone visits the squirrel then they are round.
If someone chases the rabbit then the rabbit is round.
If someone is round then they like the dog.
If the squirrel likes the bald eagle and the squirrel is not round then the bald eagle likes the rabbit.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The rabbit does not like the dog.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate each premise and the conclusion into FOL expressions and evaluate whether the conclusion logically follows from the premises.

### Premises
1. **The bald eagle chases the dog.**
   FOL: Chases(BaldEagle, Dog)

2. **The bald eagle is green.**
   FOL: Green(BaldEagle)

3. **The bald eagle visits the squirrel.**
   FOL: Visits(BaldEagle, Squirrel)

4. **The dog chases the rabbit.**
   FOL: Chases(Dog, Rabbit)

5. **The dog likes the squirrel.**
   FOL: Likes(Dog, Squirrel)

6. **The rabbit chases the bald eagle.**
   FOL: Chases(Rabbit, BaldEagle)

7. **The rabbit is rough.**
   FOL: Rough(Rabbit)

8. **The rabbit likes the squirrel.**
   FOL: Likes(Rabbit, Squirrel)

9. **The rabbit visits the squirrel.**
   FOL: Visits(Rabbit, Squirrel)

10. **The squirrel likes the bald eagle.**
    FOL: Likes(Squirrel, BaldEagle)

11. **If someone likes the dog then the dog is round.**
    FOL: all x. (Likes(x, Dog) -> Round(Dog))

12. **If someone chases the rabbit then the rabbit does not visit the dog.**
    FOL: all x. (Chases(x, Rabbit) -> -Visits(Rabbit, Dog))

13. **If someone likes the dog then they are rough.**
    FOL: all x. (Likes(x, Dog) -> Rough(x))

14. **If someone likes the dog then they are green.**
    FOL: all x. (Likes(x, Dog) -> Green(x))

15. **If someone visits the squirrel then they are round.**
    FOL: all x. (Visits(x, Squirrel) -> Round(x))

16. **If someone chases the rabbit then the rabbit is round.**
    FOL: all x. (Chases(x, Rabbit) -> Round(Rabbit))

17. **If someone is round then they like the dog.**
    FOL: all x. (Round(x) -> Likes(x, Dog))

18. **If the squirrel likes the bald eagle and the squirrel is not round then the bald eagle likes the rabbit.**
    FOL: (Likes(Squirrel, BaldEagle) & -Round(Squirrel)) -> Likes(BaldEagle, Rabbit)

### Conclusion
**The rabbit does not like the dog.**
FOL: -Likes(Rabbit, Dog)

### Evaluation

Firstly, we need to see if any of the premises directly or indirectly lead us to conclude that the rabbit does not like the dog.

From the premises:
- We know that the dog chases the rabbit (Premise 4).
- From Premise 12, since the dog chases the rabbit, the rabbit does not visit the dog. However, this does not directly affect whether the rabbit likes the dog.
- From Premise 13, if someone likes the dog, they must be rough. Since the rabbit is already rough (Premise 7), it could potentially like the dog.
- From Premise 14, if someone likes the dog, they must be green. The rabbit is not specified to be green, so this does not help us conclude anything about the rabbit liking the dog.
- From Premise 15, if someone visits the squirrel, they are round. The rabbit visits the squirrel (Premise 9), so the rabbit must be round.
- From Premise 17, if someone is round, they like the dog. Since the rabbit is round (from Premise 15), it follows that the rabbit likes the dog.

Thus, based on the premises, we can infer that the rabbit does like the dog, which contradicts the conclusion that the rabbit does not like the dog.

Therefore, the answer is:

**ANSWER: False**

The conclusion "The rabbit does not like the dog" does not follow from the premises; in fact, the premises suggest that the rabbit does like the dog.
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 87 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
FOL: all x. (Taxpayer(x) -> ContributeTo(x, Country))

TEXT: Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
FOL: all x. (SentencedForMurder(x) -> Imprisoned(x))
TEXT: Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
FOL: all x. (Imprisoned((x) -> Has(x, CriminalRecord))

TEXT: James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
FOL: ((Has(James, CriminalRecord) & -Taxpayer(James)) | (-Has(James, CriminalRecord) & Taxpayer(James)))
TEXT: James does not contribute to the country.
FOL: ContributeToCountry(James)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Anne is nice.
Bob is cold.
Bob is not red.
Bob is rough.
Charlie is red.
Charlie is rough.
Harry is nice.
Harry is quiet.
Harry is rough.
Harry is round.
Nice people are quiet.
If someone is red and nice then they are not quiet.
Quiet people are cold.
If someone is quiet and round then they are not red.
If someone is green and quiet then they are round.
If someone is cold then they are green.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Bob is round.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the premises and the conclusion using first-order logic (FOL):

### Premises
1. **Anne is nice.**
   - FOL: Nice(Anne)
2. **Bob is cold.**
   - FOL: Cold(Bob)
3. **Bob is not red.**
   - FOL: -Red(Bob)
4. **Bob is rough.**
   - FOL: Rough(Bob)
5. **Charlie is red.**
   - FOL: Red(Charlie)
6. **Charlie is rough.**
   - FOL: Rough(Charlie)
7. **Harry is nice.**
   - FOL: Nice(Harry)
8. **Harry is quiet.**
   - FOL: Quiet(Harry)
9. **Harry is rough.**
   - FOL: Rough(Harry)
10. **Harry is round.**
    - FOL: Round(Harry)
11. **Nice people are quiet.**
    - FOL: all x. (Nice(x) -> Quiet(x))
12. **If someone is red and nice then they are not quiet.**
    - FOL: all x. ((Red(x) & Nice(x)) -> -Quiet(x))
13. **Quiet people are cold.**
    - FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) -> Cold(x))
14. **If someone is quiet and round then they are not red.**
    - FOL: all x. ((Quiet(x) & Round(x)) -> -Red(x))
15. **If someone is green and quiet then they are round.**
    - FOL: all x. ((Green(x) & Quiet(x)) -> Round(x))
16. **If someone is cold then they are green.**
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) -> Green(x))

### Conclusion
- **Bob is round.**
  - FOL: Round(Bob)

### Evaluation
From the premises:
- Bob is cold (Cold(Bob)).
- By premise 16, if someone is cold, they are green (Cold(Bob) -> Green(Bob)).
- By premise 13, if someone is quiet, they are cold (Quiet(x) -> Cold(x)). Since Bob is cold, we cannot infer that Bob is quiet directly unless we have additional information about Bob being quiet.
- We do not have any direct information suggesting Bob is quiet or round.
- There is no information provided about Bob's roundness.

Therefore, based on the given premises, there is no evidence to support that Bob is round.

**ANSWER: False**

This is because none of the premises provide a direct or indirect link that would allow us to conclude that Bob is round.
Processed: False

Reference: Uncertain
========================================
