<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
FOL: all x. (Taxpayer(x) -> ContributeTo(x, Country))
TEXT: Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
FOL: all x. (WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency) -> Taxpayer(x))
TEXT: Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
FOL: all x. (ServesIn(x, TheArmy) -> WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency))
TEXT: Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
FOL: all x. (SentencedForMurder(x) -> Imprisoned(x))
TEXT: Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
FOL: all x. (Imprisoned((x) -> Has(x, CriminalRecord))
TEXT: James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
FOL: ((SentencedForMurder(James) & -Imprisoned(James)) | (-SentencedForMurder(James) & Imprisoned(James)))
TEXT: James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
FOL: ((Has(James, CriminalRecord) & -Taxpayer(James)) | (-Has(James, CriminalRecord) & Taxpayer(James)))
TEXT: James does not contribute to the country.
FOL: ContributeToCountry(James)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: Every chef can cook.
FOL: all x. (Chef(x) -> Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
FOL: exists x. (-Chef(x) & Can(x, Cook))
TEXT: People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
FOL: all x. (Can(x, Cook) -> (CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(x, Pasta)))
TEXT: If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
FOL: all x. (CanMake(x, Cookies) & CanMake(x, Muffins) -> Baker(x))
TEXT: Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
FOL: all x. ((Baker(x) & CanMake(x, ScrambledEggs)) -> CanMake(x, GoodBreakfast))
TEXT: Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
FOL: CanMake(Luke, Cookies) & (CanMake(Luke, ScrambledEggs) & CanMake(Luke, Muffins) & -CanMake(Luke, Pasta)
TEXT: Luke is a chef.
FOL: MakeGoodBreakfast(Luke)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
FOL: exists x. exists y. (Develop(eTS, x) & Develop(eTS, y) & StandardizedTest(x) & StandardizedTest(y) & In(x, UnitedState) & In(y, UnitedState) & For(x, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation) & For(y, kOneTwoAndHigherEducation))
TEXT: ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
FOL: exists x. (Administer(eTS, x) & InternationalTest(x) & (TOEFL(x) | TOEIC(x) | GRE(x) | SubjectTest(x)))
TEXT: Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.

FOL: exists x. (Develop(eTS, x) & StateWideAssesment(x) & UsedFor(x, AccountabilityTesting))
TEXT: ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
FOL: exists x. (Develops(Ets, x) & For(x, k-OneTwoandhighereducation)) & exists x. (Develops(Ets, x) & AssociatedWith(x, Entrytouseducationinstitutions))

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.

TEXT: Musicals on Broadway are not films.

TEXT: Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Anne is big.
Anne is cold.
Dave is quiet.
Dave is smart.
Gary is big.
Gary is cold.
Gary is quiet.
Gary is not red.
Gary is rough.
Gary is round.
Harry is red.
Harry is rough.
Big things are cold.
Round, rough things are cold.
If something is cold then it is rough.
If something is big and cold then it is quiet.
If something is cold then it is quiet.
Quiet things are round.
Round, cold things are big.
Red, rough things are big.
All round things are smart.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Dave is not cold.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the given premises and conclusion into First Order Logic (FOL) and then evaluate the conclusion based on the premises.

### Translation

**Premises**

1. **Anne is big.**
   - FOL: Big(Anne)
   
2. **Anne is cold.**
   - FOL: Cold(Anne)
   
3. **Dave is quiet.**
   - FOL: Quiet(Dave)
   
4. **Dave is smart.**
   - FOL: Smart(Dave)
   
5. **Gary is big.**
   - FOL: Big(Gary)
   
6. **Gary is cold.**
   - FOL: Cold(Gary)
   
7. **Gary is quiet.**
   - FOL: Quiet(Gary)
   
8. **Gary is not red.**
   - FOL: -Red(Gary)
   
9. **Gary is rough.**
   - FOL: Rough(Gary)
   
10. **Gary is round.**
    - FOL: Round(Gary)
    
11. **Harry is red.**
    - FOL: Red(Harry)
    
12. **Harry is rough.**
    - FOL: Rough(Harry)
    
13. **Big things are cold.**
    - FOL: all x. (Big(x) -> Cold(x))
    
14. **Round, rough things are cold.**
    - FOL: all x. (Round(x) & Rough(x) -> Cold(x))
    
15. **If something is cold then it is rough.**
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) -> Rough(x))
    
16. **If something is big and cold then it is quiet.**
    - FOL: all x. (Big(x) & Cold(x) -> Quiet(x))
    
17. **If something is cold then it is quiet.**
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) -> Quiet(x))
    
18. **Quiet things are round.**
    - FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) -> Round(x))
    
19. **Round, cold things are big.**
    - FOL: all x. (Round(x) & Cold(x) -> Big(x))
    
20. **Red, rough things are big.**
    - FOL: all x. (Red(x) & Rough(x) -> Big(x))
    
21. **All round things are smart.**
    - FOL: all x. (Round(x) -> Smart(x))
    
**Conclusion**

22. **Dave is not cold.**
    - FOL: -Cold(Dave)

### Evaluation

We need to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.

1. **Given that Dave is quiet:** 
   - FOL: Quiet(Dave)
   
2. From premise 18 (Quiet things are round), we know:
   - FOL: Quiet(Dave) -> Round(Dave)
   
3. From premise 21 (All round things are smart), we know:
   - FOL: Round(Dave) -> Smart(Dave)
   
   Since Dave is already known to be smart, this holds true.

4. From premise 17 (If something is cold then it is quiet):
   - FOL: Cold(x) -> Quiet(x)
   
   Since Dave is quiet, this does not necessarily imply he is cold. However, it does mean that if Dave were cold, he would indeed be quiet.

5. We need to check if there is any direct or indirect information suggesting Dave is cold. The premises do not provide any such information directly about Dave being cold or not cold.

6. There is no explicit statement or inference chain from the premises that definitively establishes Dave’s temperature state (cold or not cold).

Thus, based on the provided premises, there is insufficient information to conclude definitively whether Dave is cold or not cold.

**Final Answer:**

ANSWER: Uncertain
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain

=== Example 89 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))

FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Anne is green.
Anne is nice.
Anne is quiet.
Erin is big.
Erin is nice.
Erin is quiet.
Gary is blue.
Gary is green.
Harry is blue.
Harry is green.

Harry is round.

Nice things are round.
If something is round then it is quiet.

Nice things are big.
If something is round and quiet then it is kind.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Harry is not blue.
</CONCLUSION>

Let's analyze the premises and the conclusion step-by-step using the provided rules and information.

### Premises
1. **Anne is green.**
   - `Green(Anne)`
2. **Anne is nice.**
   - `Nice(Anne)`
3. **Anne is quiet.**
   - `Quiet(Anne)`
4. **Erin is big.**
   - `Big(Erin)`
5. **Erin is nice.**
   - `Nice(Erin)`
6. **Erin is quiet.**
   - `Quiet(Erin)`
7. **Gary is blue.**
   - `Blue(Gary)`
8. **Gary is green.**
   - `Green(Gary)`
9. **Harry is blue.**
   - `Blue(Harry)`
10. **Harry is green.**
    - `Green(Harry)`
11. **Harry is kind.**
    - `Kind(Harry)`
12. **Harry is round.**
    - `Round(Harry)`
13. **If something is kind and blue then it is nice.**
    - `all x. (Kind(x) & Blue(x) -> Nice(x))`
14. **Nice things are round.**
    - `all x. (Nice(x) -> Round(x))`
15. **If something is round then it is quiet.**
    - `all x. (Round(x) -> Quiet(x))`
16. **Blue things are round.**
    - `all x. (Blue(x) -> Round(x))`
17. **Nice things are big.**
    - `all x. (Nice(x) -> Big(x))`
18. **If something is round and quiet then it is kind.**
    - `all x. (Round(x) & Quiet(x) -> Kind(x))`

### Conclusion
**Harry is not blue.**
- `Not Blue(Harry)`

### Analysis

We need to check if `Not Blue(Harry)` follows from the premises. 

Given:
- `Blue(Harry)` (Premise 9)
- `Round(Harry)` (Premise 12)
- `Quiet(Harry)` (From `Round(Harry)` and Premise 15: `all x. (Round(x) -> Quiet(x))`)
- `Kind(Harry)` (Premise 11)

Now, let's verify these properties with the rules:

- Since `Blue(Harry)` is true, `Round(Harry)` must be true according to Premise 16 (`all x. (Blue(x) -> Round(x))`).
- Given `Round(Harry)`, and since `Round(Harry)` implies `Quiet(Harry)` (Premise 15), we know that `Quiet(Harry)` is true.
- With `Round(Harry)` and `Quiet(Harry)` being true, `Kind(Harry)` should be true according to Premise 18 (`all x. (Round(x) & Quiet(x) -> Kind(x))`). This matches our premise (11).

Since all conditions align with the given rules, the premises do not support the conclusion that `Not Blue(Harry)`.

Therefore, the evaluation of the conclusion "Harry is not blue" given the premises is:

```
ANSWER: False
```

=== Example 90 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.

<CONCLUSION>

TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.

Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Anne is blue.
Erin is quiet.
Fiona is big.
Fiona is furry.
Fiona is nice.
Harry is furry.
Harry is not rough.
Round things are blue.
If something is round and not big then it is not nice.
Quiet things are nice.
All blue, round things are nice.
Nice, rough things are round.
If something is furry then it is round.
Furry, blue things are quiet.
Nice things are furry.
If something is round and blue then it is not rough.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Erin is not blue.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the given premises and see if we can conclude that Erin is not blue.

### Premises:
1. **Anne is blue.**
   - \( Blue(Anne) \)

2. **Erin is quiet.**
   - \( Quiet(Erin) \)

3. **Fiona is big.**
   - \( Big(Fiona) \)

4. **Fiona is furry.**
   - \( Furry(Fiona) \)

5. **Fiona is nice.**
   - \( Nice(Fiona) \)

6. **Harry is furry.**
   - \( Furry(Harry) \)

7. **Harry is not rough.**
   - \( -Rough(Harry) \)

8. **Round things are blue.**
   - \( Round(x) \rightarrow Blue(x) \)

9. **If something is round and not big, then it is not nice.**
   - \( Round(x) \land -Big(x) \rightarrow -Nice(x) \)

10. **Quiet things are nice.**
    - \( Quiet(x) \rightarrow Nice(x) \)

11. **All blue, round things are nice.**
    - \( Blue(x) \land Round(x) \rightarrow Nice(x) \)

12. **Nice, rough things are round.**
    - \( Nice(x) \land Rough(x) \rightarrow Round(x) \)

13. **If something is furry, then it is round.**
    - \( Furry(x) \rightarrow Round(x) \)

14. **Furry, blue things are quiet.**
    - \( Furry(x) \land Blue(x) \rightarrow Quiet(x) \)

15. **Nice things are furry.**
    - \( Nice(x) \rightarrow Furry(x) \)

16. **If something is round and blue, then it is not rough.**
    - \( Round(x) \land Blue(x) \rightarrow -Rough(x) \)

### Conclusion:
**Erin is not blue.**
- \( -Blue(Erin) \)

### Analysis:

From premise 2, we know that Erin is quiet:
- \( Quiet(Erin) \)

From premise 10, quiet things are nice:
- \( Quiet(x) \rightarrow Nice(x) \)
Thus, since Erin is quiet, Erin must be nice:
- \( Nice(Erin) \)

From premise 15, nice things are furry:
- \( Nice(x) \rightarrow Furry(x) \)
Thus, since Erin is nice, Erin must be furry:
- \( Furry(Erin) \)

From premise 13, if something is furry, then it is round:
- \( Furry(x) \rightarrow Round(x) \)
Thus, since Erin is furry, Erin must be round:
- \( Round(Erin) \)

From premise 8, round things are blue:
- \( Round(x) \rightarrow Blue(x) \)
Thus, since Erin is round, Erin must be blue:
- \( Blue(Erin) \)

However, the conclusion we need to verify is:
- \( -Blue(Erin) \)

Based on the logical implications derived from the premises, we find that Erin must be blue because she is round and round things are blue. Therefore, the conclusion that Erin is not blue contradicts the derived information from the premises.

### Final Answer:
**ANSWER: False**

Erin being blue is a necessary consequence of the premises provided. Thus, Erin cannot be not blue based on the given information.
Processed: False

Reference: False

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

If something is big then it likes the rabbit.
If something likes the rabbit then it is rough.

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises and the conclusion step-by-step.

### Premises Analysis

1. **The cat eats the rabbit.**
   - `CatEats(Cat, Rabbit)`
   
2. **The cat is round.**
   - `IsRound(Cat)`
   
3. **The cat likes the dog.**
   - `Likes(Cat, Dog)`
   
4. **The cat needs the dog.**
   - `Needs(Cat, Dog)`
   
5. **The dog eats the cat.**
   - `DogEats(Dog, Cat)`
   
6. **The dog is big.**
   - `IsBig(Dog)`
   
7. **The dog likes the cat.**
   - `Likes(Dog, Cat)`
   
8. **The dog likes the rabbit.**
   - `Likes(Dog, Rabbit)`
   
9. **The dog needs the mouse.**
   - `Needs(Dog, Mouse)`
   
10. **The mouse eats the cat.**
    - `MouseEats(Mouse, Cat)`
    
11. **The mouse needs the cat.**
    - `Needs(Mouse, Cat)`
    
12. **The rabbit eats the cat.**
    - `RabbitEats(Rabbit, Cat)`
    
13. **The rabbit is big.**
    - `IsBig(Rabbit)`
    
14. **The rabbit is rough.**
    - `IsRough(Rabbit)`
    
15. **The rabbit needs the cat.**
    - `Needs(Rabbit, Cat)`
    
16. **The rabbit needs the dog.**
    - `Needs(Rabbit, Dog)`
    
17. **If something likes the dog then the dog eats the cat.**
    - `all x. (Likes(x, Dog) -> DogEats(Dog, Cat))`
    
18. **If the dog is rough then the dog eats the cat.**
    - `if IsRough(Dog) then DogEats(Dog, Cat)`
    
19. **If something eats the cat and the cat likes the rabbit then it is big.**
    - `all x. (Eats(x, Cat) & Likes(Cat, Rabbit) -> IsBig(x))`
    
20. **If something is kind then it likes the cat.**
    - `all x. (IsKind(x) -> Likes(x, Cat))`
    
21. **If something likes the rabbit and the rabbit eats the cat then the cat is big.**
    - `all x. (Likes(x, Rabbit) & RabbitEats(Rabbit, Cat) -> IsBig(Cat))`
    
22. **If the rabbit is big then the rabbit eats the cat.**
    - `if IsBig(Rabbit) then RabbitEats(Rabbit, Cat)`
    
23. **If something needs the cat then it is round.**
    - `all x. (Needs(x, Cat) -> IsRound(x))`
    
24. **If something is big then it likes the rabbit.**
    - `all x. (IsBig(x) -> Likes(x, Rabbit))`
    
25. **If something likes the rabbit then it is rough.**
    - `all x. (Likes(x, Rabbit) -> IsRough(x))`

### Conclusion

**The mouse likes the cat.**
- `Likes(Mouse, Cat)`

### Evaluation

From the premises:
- `Needs(Mouse, Cat)` (Premise 11).
- By premise 23, if something needs the cat, then it is round. Therefore, `IsRound(Mouse)`.
- There is no direct premise that says `Likes(Mouse, Cat)`, and no chain of reasoning directly leads to the conclusion based on the provided information.

Given this analysis:

**ANSWER: Uncertain**

The conclusion "The mouse likes the cat" cannot be definitively derived from the given premises.

=== Example 93 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.

TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))

FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.

One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.

Musicals on Broadway are not films.

TEXT: Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
FOL: exists x. (BRICS(x) & Speaks(x, Hindi))

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Bob is green.
Bob is rough.
Bob is white.
Charlie is rough.
Dave is quiet.
Gary is cold.
Gary is rough.
All quiet, kind people are young.
If Charlie is quiet and Charlie is young then Charlie is kind.
All green, white people are cold.
All quiet people are rough.
All rough, green people are white.
All young people are green.
Rough people are young.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Dave is not young.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the premises and conclusion into First-Order Logic (FOL) and evaluate the conclusion.

### Premises
1. **Bob is green.**
   FOL: Green(Bob)
2. **Bob is rough.**
   FOL: Rough(Bob)
3. **Bob is white.**
   FOL: White(Bob)
4. **Charlie is rough.**
   FOL: Rough(Charlie)
5. **Dave is quiet.**
   FOL: Quiet(Dave)
6. **Gary is cold.**
   FOL: Cold(Gary)
7. **Gary is rough.**
   FOL: Rough(Gary)
8. **All quiet, kind people are young.**
   FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) & Kind(x) -> Young(x))
9. **If Charlie is quiet and Charlie is young then Charlie is kind.**
   FOL: (Quiet(Charlie) & Young(Charlie) -> Kind(Charlie))
10. **All green, white people are cold.**
    FOL: all x. (Green(x) & White(x) -> Cold(x))
11. **All quiet people are rough.**
    FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) -> Rough(x))
12. **All rough, green people are white.**
    FOL: all x. (Rough(x) & Green(x) -> White(x))
13. **All young people are green.**
    FOL: all x. (Young(x) -> Green(x))
14. **Rough people are young.**
    FOL: all x. (Rough(x) -> Young(x))

### Conclusion
**Dave is not young.**
FOL: -Young(Dave)

### Evaluation

We know that:
- **Dave is quiet**: Quiet(Dave)
- From premise 11, since all quiet people are rough, we have: Rough(Dave)
- From premise 14, since all rough people are young, we have: Young(Dave)

Given these deductions, we see that Dave must be young because he is quiet and therefore rough, and rough people are young.

Thus, the conclusion **Dave is not young** contradicts the premises.

### Final Answer
ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.

The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
The bald eagle chases the dog.
The bald eagle eats the dog.
The bald eagle is big.
The bald eagle likes the bear.
The bear eats the dog.
The bear is kind.
The dog chases the tiger.
The dog eats the bald eagle.
The dog is kind.
The tiger chases the bear.
The tiger eats the bear.
The tiger is big.
The tiger is round.
The tiger is young.
If someone is kind then they chase the bald eagle.
If someone chases the bear and the bear likes the tiger then they eat the bald eagle.
If someone is kind then they eat the bald eagle.
If someone likes the dog then they like the tiger.
If someone likes the tiger then they are young.
If someone eats the dog then the dog is big.
If someone eats the bald eagle then they like the dog.
If someone likes the dog and they do not chase the tiger then the dog chases the bald eagle.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The dog does not like the tiger.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the premises and analyze the conclusion step-by-step.

### Premises

1. **The bald eagle chases the dog.**
   - FOL: Chases(BaldEagle, Dog)

2. **The bald eagle eats the dog.**
   - FOL: Eats(BaldEagle, Dog)

3. **The bald eagle is big.**
   - FOL: Big(BaldEagle)

4. **The bald eagle likes the bear.**
   - FOL: Likes(BaldEagle, Bear)

5. **The bear eats the dog.**
   - FOL: Eats(Bear, Dog)

6. **The bear is kind.**
   - FOL: Kind(Bear)

7. **The dog chases the tiger.**
   - FOL: Chases(Dog, Tiger)

8. **The dog eats the bald eagle.**
   - FOL: Eats(Dog, BaldEagle)

9. **The dog is kind.**
   - FOL: Kind(Dog)

10. **The tiger chases the bear.**
    - FOL: Chases(Tiger, Bear)

11. **The tiger eats the bear.**
    - FOL: Eats(Tiger, Bear)

12. **The tiger is big.**
    - FOL: Big(Tiger)

13. **The tiger is round.**
    - FOL: Round(Tiger)

14. **The tiger is young.**
    - FOL: Young(Tiger)

15. **If someone is kind then they chase the bald eagle.**
    - FOL: all x. (Kind(x) -> Chases(x, BaldEagle))

16. **If someone chases the bear and the bear likes the tiger then they eat the bald eagle.**
    - FOL: all x. (Chases(x, Bear) & Likes(Bear, Tiger) -> Eats(x, BaldEagle))

17. **If someone is kind then they eat the bald eagle.**
    - FOL: all x. (Kind(x) -> Eats(x, BaldEagle))

18. **If someone likes the dog then they like the tiger.**
    - FOL: all x. (Likes(x, Dog) -> Likes(x, Tiger))

19. **If someone likes the tiger then they are young.**
    - FOL: all x. (Likes(x, Tiger) -> Young(x))

20. **If someone eats the dog then the dog is big.**
    - FOL: all x. (Eats(x, Dog) -> Big(Dog))

21. **If someone eats the bald eagle then they like the dog.**
    - FOL: all x. (Eats(x, BaldEagle) -> Likes(x, Dog))

22. **If someone likes the dog and they do not chase the tiger then the dog chases the bald eagle.**
    - FOL: all x. (Likes(x, Dog) & -Chases(x, Tiger) -> Chases(Dog, BaldEagle))

### Conclusion

**The dog does not like the tiger.**

- FOL: -Likes(Dog, Tiger)

### Analysis

From the premises:
- We know that the dog is kind (Premise 9).
- By Premise 15, if someone is kind, then they chase the bald eagle. Since the dog is kind, the dog chases the bald eagle.
- By Premise 17, if someone is kind, then they eat the bald eagle. Since the dog is kind, the dog eats the bald eagle.
- By Premise 21, if someone eats the bald eagle, then they like the dog. Since the dog eats the bald eagle, the dog likes itself.
- By Premise 18, if someone likes the dog, then they like the tiger. Since the dog likes itself, it implies the dog should like the tiger.

However, the conclusion is that the dog does not like the tiger, which contradicts the derived fact that the dog likes the tiger.

Therefore, based on the given premises:

**ANSWER: False**

The dog does like the tiger according to the logical implications derived from the premises.
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 95 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

TEXT: Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
FOL: all x. (ServesIn(x, TheArmy) -> WorkFor(x, GovernmentAgency))
TEXT: Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
FOL: all x. (SentencedForMurder(x) -> Imprisoned(x))
TEXT: Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
FOL: all x. (Imprisoned((x) -> Has(x, CriminalRecord))

TEXT: James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.

TEXT: James does not contribute to the country.
FOL: ContributeToCountry(James)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.

TEXT: Luke is a chef.

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Bob is furry.
Bob is nice.
Bob is rough.
Fiona is red.
Gary is furry.
Gary is not white.
Harry is nice.
If Fiona is furry then Fiona is nice.
If Fiona is nice and Fiona is red then Fiona is furry.
All white things are red.
All white things are furry.
If something is big then it is white.
All nice things are big.
If something is furry then it is quiet.
If Fiona is not nice and Fiona is not furry then Fiona is quiet.
Big, quiet things are rough.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Harry is rough.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the premises and the conclusion into First-Order Logic (FOL):

**Premises:**
1. Bob is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Bob)
2. Bob is nice.
   - FOL: Nice(Bob)
3. Bob is rough.
   - FOL: Rough(Bob)
4. Fiona is red.
   - FOL: Red(Fiona)
5. Gary is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Gary)
6. Gary is not white.
   - FOL: -White(Gary)
7. Harry is nice.
   - FOL: Nice(Harry)
8. If Fiona is furry then Fiona is nice.
   - FOL: Furry(Fiona) -> Nice(Fiona)
9. If Fiona is nice and Fiona is red then Fiona is furry.
   - FOL: (Nice(Fiona) & Red(Fiona)) -> Furry(Fiona)
10. All white things are red.
    - FOL: all x. (White(x) -> Red(x))
11. All white things are furry.
    - FOL: all x. (White(x) -> Furry(x))
12. If something is big then it is white.
    - FOL: all x. (Big(x) -> White(x))
13. All nice things are big.
    - FOL: all x. (Nice(x) -> Big(x))
14. If something is furry then it is quiet.
    - FOL: all x. (Furry(x) -> Quiet(x))
15. If Fiona is not nice and Fiona is not furry then Fiona is quiet.
    - FOL: (-Nice(Fiona) & -Furry(Fiona)) -> Quiet(Fiona)
16. Big, quiet things are rough.
    - FOL: all x. ((Big(x) & Quiet(x)) -> Rough(x))

**Conclusion:**
- Harry is rough.
- FOL: Rough(Harry)

Now, let's evaluate the conclusion based on the premises.

From premise 7:
- Nice(Harry)

From premise 13:
- Nice(Harry) -> Big(Harry)
Since Harry is nice, he must be big:
- Big(Harry)

From premise 12:
- Big(Harry) -> White(Harry)
Since Harry is big, he must be white:
- White(Harry)

From premise 11:
- White(Harry) -> Furry(Harry)
Since Harry is white, he must be furry:
- Furry(Harry)

From premise 14:
- Furry(Harry) -> Quiet(Harry)
Since Harry is furry, he must be quiet:
- Quiet(Harry)

From premise 16:
- (Big(Harry) & Quiet(Harry)) -> Rough(Harry)
Since Harry is both big and quiet, he must be rough:
- Rough(Harry)

Therefore, the conclusion that "Harry is rough" logically follows from the premises.

**ANSWER: True**
Processed: True

Reference: True

<PREMISES>
The cow chases the rabbit.
The cow needs the squirrel.
The dog chases the rabbit.
The dog needs the cow.
The dog sees the cow.
The rabbit chases the cow.
The rabbit chases the squirrel.
The rabbit needs the cow.
The rabbit needs the dog.
The rabbit needs the squirrel.
The rabbit sees the dog.
The squirrel chases the rabbit.
The squirrel needs the rabbit.
The squirrel sees the dog.
If something needs the dog and the dog needs the squirrel then the squirrel is nice.
If something is green and nice then it needs the cow.
Nice things are green.
If something is green then it chases the cow.
If something needs the cow then it sees the squirrel.
If something is kind and it sees the dog then the dog needs the cow.
If something sees the rabbit then it needs the squirrel.
If something needs the cow then it needs the squirrel.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The squirrel sees the squirrel.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
To solve this problem, we need to carefully analyze each premise and see if we can logically deduce the conclusion "The squirrel sees the squirrel."

Let's translate the premises into FOL:

1. The cow chases the rabbit.
   - FOL: Chases(Cow, Rabbit)
2. The cow needs the squirrel.
   - FOL: Needs(Cow, Squirrel)
3. The dog chases the rabbit.
   - FOL: Chases(Dog, Rabbit)
4. The dog needs the cow.
   - FOL: Needs(Dog, Cow)
5. The dog sees the cow.
   - FOL: Sees(Dog, Cow)
6. The rabbit chases the cow.
   - FOL: Chases(Rabbit, Cow)
7. The rabbit chases the squirrel.
   - FOL: Chases(Rabbit, Squirrel)
8. The rabbit needs the cow.
   - FOL: Needs(Rabbit, Cow)
9. The rabbit needs the dog.
   - FOL: Needs(Rabbit, Dog)
10. The rabbit needs the squirrel.
    - FOL: Needs(Rabbit, Squirrel)
11. The rabbit sees the dog.
    - FOL: Sees(Rabbit, Dog)
12. The squirrel chases the rabbit.
    - FOL: Chases(Squirrel, Rabbit)
13. The squirrel needs the rabbit.
    - FOL: Needs(Squirrel, Rabbit)
14. The squirrel sees the dog.
    - FOL: Sees(Squirrel, Dog)
15. If something needs the dog and the dog needs the squirrel then the squirrel is nice.
    - FOL: all x. ((Needs(x, Dog) & Needs(Dog, Squirrel)) -> Nice(Squirrel))
16. If something is green and nice then it needs the cow.
    - FOL: all x. ((Green(x) & Nice(x)) -> Needs(x, Cow))
17. Nice things are green.
    - FOL: all x. (Nice(x) -> Green(x))
18. If something is green then it chases the cow.
    - FOL: all x. (Green(x) -> Chases(x, Cow))
19. If something needs the cow then it sees the squirrel.
    - FOL: all x. (Needs(x, Cow) -> Sees(x, Squirrel))
20. If something is kind and it sees the dog then the dog needs the cow.
    - FOL: all x. ((Kind(x) & Sees(x, Dog)) -> Needs(Dog, Cow))
21. If something sees the rabbit then it needs the squirrel.
    - FOL: all x. (Sees(x, Rabbit) -> Needs(x, Squirrel))
22. If something needs the cow then it needs the squirrel.
    - FOL: all x. (Needs(x, Cow) -> Needs(x, Squirrel))

We want to conclude:
- The squirrel sees the squirrel.
  - FOL: Sees(Squirrel, Squirrel)

Let's check if we can derive this conclusion from the premises:

From Premise 14, we know:
- Sees(Squirrel, Dog)

From Premise 13, we know:
- Needs(Squirrel, Rabbit)

Premise 21 states:
- all x. (Sees(x, Rabbit) -> Needs(x, Squirrel))

But since Squirrel sees Dog, not Rabbit, this doesn't directly apply here.

Premise 19 states:
- all x. (Needs(x, Cow) -> Sees(x, Squirrel))

From Premise 2, we know:
- Needs(Cow, Squirrel)

However, we need to find out if Squirrel needs Cow to use Premise 19. From Premise 9, we know:
- Needs(Rabbit, Cow)

This implies:
- Needs(Squirrel, Cow) [using Premise 22]

Therefore, using Premise 19:
- Sees(Squirrel, Squirrel)

Thus, we can conclude that the squirrel sees the squirrel.

**ANSWER: True**

The squirrel sees the squirrel based on the logical deductions from the premises provided.
Processed: True

Reference: True

=== Example 97 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Bob is not furry.
Bob is young.
Erin is red.
Erin is young.
Fiona is blue.
Harry is blue.
Harry is not rough.
If something is nice and young then it is furry.
If something is blue and not rough then it is furry.
All blue things are furry.
All rough, blue things are nice.
All cold, furry things are nice.
Furry things are cold.
If something is blue and red then it is cold.
Young things are red.
All nice things are young.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Fiona is not furry.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the premises and conclusion into FOL expressions and evaluate the conclusion based on these premises.

### Premises

1. **Bob is not furry.**
   FOL: -Furry(Bob)
2. **Bob is young.**
   FOL: Young(Bob)
3. **Erin is red.**
   FOL: Red(Erin)
4. **Erin is young.**
   FOL: Young(Erin)
5. **Fiona is blue.**
   FOL: Blue(Fiona)
6. **Harry is blue.**
   FOL: Blue(Harry)
7. **Harry is not rough.**
   FOL: -Rough(Harry)
8. **If something is nice and young then it is furry.**
   FOL: all x. (Nice(x) & Young(x) -> Furry(x))
9. **If something is blue and not rough then it is furry.**
   FOL: all x. (Blue(x) & -Rough(x) -> Furry(x))
10. **All blue things are furry.**
    FOL: all x. (Blue(x) -> Furry(x))
11. **All rough, blue things are nice.**
    FOL: all x. (Rough(x) & Blue(x) -> Nice(x))
12. **All cold, furry things are nice.**
    FOL: all x. (Cold(x) & Furry(x) -> Nice(x))
13. **Furry things are cold.**
    FOL: all x. (Furry(x) -> Cold(x))
14. **If something is blue and red then it is cold.**
    FOL: all x. (Blue(x) & Red(x) -> Cold(x))
15. **Young things are red.**
    FOL: all x. (Young(x) -> Red(x))
16. **All nice things are young.**
    FOL: all x. (Nice(x) -> Young(x))

### Conclusion
**Fiona is not furry.**
FOL: -Furry(Fiona)

### Evaluation

From the premises:
- Fiona is blue: Blue(Fiona)
- All blue things are furry: all x. (Blue(x) -> Furry(x))

Given that Fiona is blue, and all blue things are furry, we can infer:
- Furry(Fiona)

Therefore, Fiona is furry, which directly contradicts the conclusion that Fiona is not furry.

### Final Answer
ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False

TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Bob is furry.
Bob is young.
Charlie is red.
Dave is blue.
Dave is cold.
Dave is furry.
Gary is young.
If Gary is rough and Gary is young then Gary is quiet.
All quiet things are red.
Young, blue things are red.
Furry, rough things are red.
Red things are rough.
All young, rough things are cold.
If something is rough and not young then it is cold.
If something is cold then it is furry.
All young things are quiet.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Dave is not quiet.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the premises and the conclusion into first-order logic (FOL) expressions:

**Premises:**
1. Bob is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Bob)
2. Bob is young.
   - FOL: Young(Bob)
3. Charlie is red.
   - FOL: Red(Charlie)
4. Dave is blue.
   - FOL: Blue(Dave)
5. Dave is cold.
   - FOL: Cold(Dave)
6. Dave is furry.
   - FOL: Furry(Dave)
7. Gary is young.
   - FOL: Young(Gary)
8. If Gary is rough and Gary is young then Gary is quiet.
   - FOL: (Rough(Gary) & Young(Gary)) -> Quiet(Gary)
9. All quiet things are red.
   - FOL: all x. (Quiet(x) -> Red(x))
10. Young, blue things are red.
    - FOL: all x. (Young(x) & Blue(x) -> Red(x))
11. Furry, rough things are red.
    - FOL: all x. (Furry(x) & Rough(x) -> Red(x))
12. Red things are rough.
    - FOL: all x. (Red(x) -> Rough(x))
13. All young, rough things are cold.
    - FOL: all x. (Young(x) & Rough(x) -> Cold(x))
14. If something is rough and not young then it is cold.
    - FOL: all x. (Rough(x) & -Young(x) -> Cold(x))
15. If something is cold then it is furry.
    - FOL: all x. (Cold(x) -> Furry(x))
16. All young things are quiet.
    - FOL: all x. (Young(x) -> Quiet(x))

**Conclusion:**
- Dave is not quiet.
  - FOL: -Quiet(Dave)

Now let's evaluate the conclusion based on the premises.

From premise 5, we know that Dave is cold:
- FOL: Cold(Dave)

According to premise 15, if something is cold, it is furry:
- FOL: Cold(Dave) -> Furry(Dave)

We already know from premise 6 that Dave is furry:
- FOL: Furry(Dave)

Next, we look at premise 16, which states that all young things are quiet:
- FOL: all x. (Young(x) -> Quiet(x))

However, there is no information about whether Dave is young. Therefore, we cannot directly apply this rule to Dave. We need to consider other rules.

From premise 14, if something is rough and not young, then it is cold:
- FOL: all x. (Rough(x) & -Young(x) -> Cold(x))

Given that Dave is cold, if Dave were rough and not young, this would hold. But we do not have information about Dave being rough. 

Premise 15 states that if something is cold, it is furry:
- FOL: Cold(Dave) -> Furry(Dave)

Since Dave is cold and therefore furry, we must check if this makes him quiet.

Premise 16 states that all young things are quiet:
- FOL: all x. (Young(x) -> Quiet(x))

We need to determine if Dave is young. Since there is no direct statement about Dave being young, we must infer based on other premises.

Considering all premises, we do not have sufficient information to conclude that Dave is quiet or not quiet definitively because we do not have information about Dave's youthfulness and roughness.

Therefore, the conclusion "Dave is not quiet" is uncertain based on the provided premises.

**Answer: Uncertain**
Processed: Uncertain

=== Example 99 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.

Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
The bald eagle chases the cow.
The bald eagle likes the rabbit.
The bald eagle visits the cow.
The cow is not young.
The mouse chases the rabbit.
The mouse likes the bald eagle.
The mouse likes the cow.
The mouse does not like the rabbit.
The rabbit chases the mouse.
The rabbit is kind.
The rabbit is young.
The rabbit likes the cow.
If something is round then it chases the rabbit.
If something chases the cow then it is young.
If the bald eagle likes the rabbit and the rabbit chases the cow then the bald eagle does not visit the cow.
If the bald eagle chases the rabbit then the rabbit is round.
If something is young and it likes the rabbit then it is green.
If something is green then it is round.
If the rabbit likes the bald eagle then the bald eagle is round.
If something chases the bald eagle then it likes the bald eagle.
If something is green and it likes the cow then it visits the rabbit.

<CONCLUSION>
The mouse likes the rabbit.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's translate the given premises and the conclusion into first-order logic (FOL) expressions and then evaluate the conclusion based on the premises.

**Premises:**

1. The bald eagle chases the cow.
   - FOL: Chases(BaldEagle, Cow)
2. The bald eagle likes the rabbit.
   - FOL: Likes(BaldEagle, Rabbit)
3. The bald eagle visits the cow.
   - FOL: Visits(BaldEagle, Cow)
4. The cow is not young.
   - FOL: -Young(Cow)
5. The mouse chases the rabbit.
   - FOL: Chases(Mouse, Rabbit)
6. The mouse likes the bald eagle.
   - FOL: Likes(Mouse, BaldEagle)
7. The mouse likes the cow.
   - FOL: Likes(Mouse, Cow)
8. The mouse does not like the rabbit.
   - FOL: -Likes(Mouse, Rabbit)
9. The rabbit chases the mouse.
   - FOL: Chases(Rabbit, Mouse)
10. The rabbit is kind.
    - FOL: Kind(Rabbit)
11. The rabbit is young.
    - FOL: Young(Rabbit)
12. The rabbit likes the cow.
    - FOL: Likes(Rabbit, Cow)
13. If something is round then it chases the rabbit.
    - FOL: all x. (Round(x) -> Chases(x, Rabbit))
14. If something chases the cow then it is young.
    - FOL: all x. (Chases(x, Cow) -> Young(x))
15. If the bald eagle likes the rabbit and the rabbit chases the cow then the bald eagle does not visit the cow.
    - FOL: (Likes(BaldEagle, Rabbit) & Chases(Rabbit, Cow)) -> -Visits(BaldEagle, Cow)
16. If the bald eagle chases the rabbit then the rabbit is round.
    - FOL: Chases(BaldEagle, Rabbit) -> Round(Rabbit)
17. If something is young and it likes the rabbit then it is green.
    - FOL: all x. ((Young(x) & Likes(x, Rabbit)) -> Green(x))
18. If something is green then it is round.
    - FOL: all x. (Green(x) -> Round(x))
19. If the rabbit likes the bald eagle then the bald eagle is round.
    - FOL: Likes(Rabbit, BaldEagle) -> Round(BaldEagle)
20. If something chases the bald eagle then it likes the bald eagle.
    - FOL: all x. (Chases(x, BaldEagle) -> Likes(x, BaldEagle))
21. If something is green and it likes the cow then it visits the rabbit.
    - FOL: all x. ((Green(x) & Likes(x, Cow)) -> Visits(x, Rabbit))

**Conclusion:**
The mouse likes the rabbit.
- FOL: Likes(Mouse, Rabbit)

Now, let's evaluate the conclusion based on the premises:

Given:
- The mouse does not like the rabbit. (Premise 8: -Likes(Mouse, Rabbit))

This directly contradicts the conclusion that the mouse likes the rabbit. Therefore, the conclusion does not follow from the premises.

**ANSWER:** False
Processed: Error
